<div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=106685817 id=\"106685817\" class=\"abstract-title\" >Abstract</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We report modelling follow-up of recently discovered gravitational-lens candidates in the Canada France Hawaii Telescope Legacy Survey. Lens modelling was done by a small group of specially interested volunteers from the Space\u2009Warps citizen\u2013science community who originally found the candidate lenses. Models are categorized according to seven diagnostics indicating (a) the image morphology and how clear or indistinct it is, (b) whether the mass map and synthetic lensed image appear to be plausible, and (c) how the lens-model mass compares with the stellar mass and the abundance-matched halo mass. The lensing masses range from \u223c10<sup>11</sup> to &gt;10<sup>13</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>. Preliminary estimates of the stellar masses show a smaller spread in stellar mass (except for two lenses): a factor of a few below or above \u223c10<sup>11</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>. Therefore, we expect the stellar-to-total mass fraction to decline sharply as lensing mass increases. The most massive system with a convincing model is J1434+522 (SW\u200905). The two low-mass outliers are J0206\u2212095 (SW\u200919) and J2217+015 (SW\u200942); if these two are indeed lenses, they probe an interesting regime of very low star formation efficiency. Some improvements to the modelling software (SpaghettiLens), and discussion of strategies regarding scaling to future surveys with more and frequent discoveries, are included.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: general&quot;\">galaxies: general</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;galaxies: stellar content&quot;\">galaxies: stellar content</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;dark matter&quot;\">dark matter</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=106685819 id=\"106685819\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">By a curious coincidence, the typical escape velocity of massive galaxies \u2013 of the order of a few hundred km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup> \u2013 is such that <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$v_{\\rm esc}^2/c^2$|\u2060</span>, expressed as an angular distance, is comparable to the apparent sizes of galaxies at cosmological distances. This coincidence is fortunate, because it makes the gravitational lensing deflection angle of distant galaxies (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$\\alpha \\sim 2v_{\\rm esc}^2/c^2$|\u2060</span>) comparable to their size on the sky. As a result, strong lensing by galaxies produces images that probe their host dark matter haloes, providing a useful tool to understand galaxy formation. While there is a general consensus about the basic mechanisms at play, involving gravitational collapse, fragmentation, and mergers of dark-matter clumps, into which gas fell, cooling through radiative processes to form dense clouds and eventually stars, there is much debate about the details (for a summary, see Silk &amp; Mamon\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>). In particular, the nature of dark matter remains mysterious: most researchers take it to be a collisionless non-relativistic fluid (cold dark matter or CDM) readily studied by simulations (for example, the influential Millennium simulation; Springel et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib39\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib39\" data-open=\"bib39\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2005</a>). However, alternative scenarios, where dark matter has exotic dynamical properties (Saxton &amp; Ferreras\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib34\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib34\" data-open=\"bib34\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Schive et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>), or is not really matter at all, but a modification of gravity (McGaugh, Lelli &amp; Schombert\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>), have also been considered.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">All this motivates the use of strong gravitational lensing over galaxy scales to study the mutual dynamics of dark matter, gas and stars. Several studies in recent years have done so (see e.g. Koopmans et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>; Leier et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Leier, Ferreras &amp; Saha\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Bruderer et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; Leier et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) but it is desirable to enlarge the samples from tens of lensing galaxies to thousands. Doing so requires both finding more lenses and also modelling their mass distribution. Recent searches through the CFHT Lens Survey (CFHTLS; Heymans et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) using arc-finders (e.g. More et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Gavazzi et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Maturi, Mizera &amp; Seidel\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Sonnenfeld et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib38\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib38\" data-open=\"bib38\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) by either machine learning methods (e.g. Paraficz et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib32\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib32\" data-open=\"bib32\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; Lanusse et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>) or visual inspection by citizen\u2013science volunteers through the Space\u2009Warps project (More et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) have, between them, discovered an average of four lenses per square degree, so one can be optimistic about finding many thousands of lenses in the next generation of wide-field surveys, from ground-based surveys such as LSST in the optical window and SKA in radio, to space-based missions such as Euclid and WFIRST (Oguri &amp; Marshall\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Collett\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). The availability of the recently published year 1 result of the Dark Energy Survey (Drlica-Wagner et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>), which covered 1800\u2009deg<sup>2</sup>, suggests that the number of lenses could grow by at least an order of magnitude within a very short time period.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The expected flood of new lens discoveries will need a similarly large modelling effort to reconstruct their mass distributions. Lens-modelling robots have started to be developed (Hezaveh, Perreault Levasseur &amp; Marshall\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Nightingale, Dye &amp; Massey\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>) but so far are able to handle only very clean systems. For typical lenses, human input is still needed. With that in mind K\u00fcng et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) developed a new modelling strategy, implemented as the SpaghettiLens<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">1</a></sup> system. The idea is to collaborate with experienced members of the citizen\u2013science community who have already participated in lens discovery through Space\u2009Warps, as well as several other projects involving astronomical data. The system was tested on a sample of simulated lenses, which were part of the training and testing set in Space\u2009Warps.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This paper follows up that study by applying SpaghettiLens to candidates discovered through Space\u2009Warps. We present results from the modelling of 58 of the 59 lens candidates reported by More et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). Each lens candidate was modelled following a collaborative refinement process, where anyone interested could improve the analysis by modifying an existing model or creating a new one. Note the difference with respect to the main Space\u2009Warps project, where volunteers from a group of \u227310<sup>4</sup> people make independent contributions. Each person is presented with a random selection of survey-patches and invited to (in effect) vote on each. The system estimates the skill level of each volunteer according to test-patches interspersed with the real data, and weights their votes accordingly (Marshall et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). There is an active forum for volunteers, but since everyone is seeing different data samples with minimal overlap, the forum has little if any influence on the votes. In SpaghettiLens, the number of volunteers is significantly lower, but the level of interaction is higher. The resulting model represents a consensus among contributors, as to the best that could be achieved with the available data and software.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We emphasize that the interpretation of the results presented here is tentative, because the systems are lens candidates at this stage, not secure lenses. Moreover the candidate-lens redshifts have large uncertainties, while the candidate-source redshifts can only be guessed at present. Nevertheless it is interesting to explore the trends observed with the already available data, based on some 300 models created by eight volunteers for 58 candidate lenses found in the 150\u2009deg<sup>2</sup> CFHTLS.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This paper is organized as follows. Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a> introduces the candidate lenses, their models and the diagnostics applied to them. The following sections elaborate on the diagnostics. Image morphology diagnostics are explained in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a> and diagnostics based on the mass models are discussed in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>. Stellar masses are presented in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>, to compare stellar and lensing masses. Finally, Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec6\"></span><a href=\"#sec6\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">6</a> summarizes and tabulates the diagnostics in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"106685826\" scrollto-destination=\"106685826\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Diagnostics of the selected models for each Space\u2009Warps candidate (see Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec6\"></span><a href=\"#sec6\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">6</a>). The full table is available online.</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table><thead><tr><th>SWID<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>ZooID<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>CFHTLS name<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>z</em><sub>lens</sub><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>Unblended<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/106685826\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">We include three appendices devoted to various technical issues relating to the modelling. The <span class=\"content-section supplementary-material\"><a path-from-xml=\"sup1\" href=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/stx3012_supp.zip?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=UiNzDmc6Ie7tX7zJPV4HozVXgKiPPJ3QRZVNcHiwP1gM3AVHcnF2KJKe78hQ4gNPw0O8Uwxc4uTlonczNekq994i9yM80hBlYEFO9Rq11vw9ohV9jJgQaYCu5DXpZFKpBWx9jNgLZC~bVGc-KtPgC1IQ5OahMgw5drFuqzT0wLU7z5zLXZND7Tf34MGcu4YdMyYIvnCrm2fAgYqIEaiDUavJ23Se1YO7xYwbJp2deU0YqF7gEOAgncZWfhQqq5iVWINuJXHI8Ianu6qtXsDUUdD2sziQWjwVUjE7X1mFfXfIvLHSayyhrwe551USLF8B955Mk~Nxmxn4Gt4ouv~gzQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\">online supplement</a></span> gives the results from all the modelled systems generated for all the lensing candidates.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=106685828 id=\"106685828\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 THE CANDIDATES AND MODELS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Space\u2009Warps is a citizen\u2013science gravitational lens search (Marshall et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). Its first run searched the CFHT Legacy Survey, a survey carried out in five optical bands (<em>u</em>*, <em>g</em>\u0384, <em>r</em>\u0384, <em>i</em>\u0384, <em>z</em>\u0384) covering a total area of 160\u2009deg<sup>2</sup> divided up into four fields W1\u2013W4. The MegaPrime camera, used for the survey, has a field of view of 1\u2009deg<sup>2</sup>, with 0.186\u2009arcsec pixels. The flux limit of the survey is <em>g</em>\u0384\u00a0&lt;\u00a025.6\u2009AB (5\u03c3) with a typical seeing FWHM \u223c0.7\u2009arcsec (Erben et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>). The cut-outs shown to the volunteers were colour composites of the <em>g</em>\u0384, <em>r</em>\u0384 and <em>i</em>\u0384 bands from randomly chosen regions. The programme resulted in 59 new lens candidates, of which 29 are considered high quality. Moreover, 82 previously known lens candidates were \u2018rediscovered\u2019. The candidates have broadly similar redshifts (0.2\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>z</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a01.0), Einstein radii between 0.7 and 5\u2009arcsec, and arc fluxes in <em>g</em>-band AB magnitudes between 22 and 26. These properties are similar to those found by previous robotic searches like ArcFinder and RingFinder (More et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">A first version of SpaghettiLens was launched in 2013 May, while the first run of Space\u2009Warps was ongoing. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> shows the total number of models generated since launch for our lens candidates. A small number of volunteers started creating models of possible lens candidates from Space\u2009Warps that were debated in the discussion forum. In the beginning of 2013 August (around day 70 since release), a modelling challenge for the candidate later to be identified as SW\u200901 was launched. A group of five volunteers presented their results in an online letter converging on a set of 30 models. In 2015 April (day 700), the first major version of SpaghettiLens was released. At the same time, the list of identified candidates was made available (as a preprint of More et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). At this stage, the volunteers were asked to create models for all the lens candidates that were still missing. The work done for candidate SW\u200929 shows that the volunteers converged on a favourable model much faster, after 15 models, generated in 30\u2009d. The total modelling effort resulted in a set of 377 SpaghettiLens models for all but one of the 59 Space\u2009Warps lens candidates; candidate SW\u200939 was not modelled by any volunteer. Over its runtime, the system logged eight major contributors (defined as volunteers that generated, at least, five models).</p>                        <a id=\"106685831\" scrollto-destination=\"106685831\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=uCfTxyEH3hf1k3~W4KdoaGaeASEATKnHARbzxRWlL04MvvQ-yN4k~GKXpV46~zBAJH2Kun6-hCgIgw78T5HuCJTpbuMNqqKmVMiIm8roNyxicSuAcYUfcK4MOkmLgo3zLxYxSO7zqRnqo0F2ein6ApMVOQry2o2-oq5RPmJbUPpCRorAAGfqHUt3BqpCCpyBo07BgPYrnGmqyS8VmSiXDdPnxxkHmN8JY4oB~xVd9eboRGcOnGFTCennCOpFWww1~6P6CYkHzMIqh~o2~ffIw~yQg6NIJb8Feun6cv16BLi7V13K~qV9zsVmIx3mMEFeRJFsU-R5XOuxrugx5Z-qOg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Number of models generated over time in days since the launch of SpaghettiLens; the black line shows all models, and the coloured lines show the five most active candidates. A total of 377 models were generated for 58 lens candidates, eight users contributed more than five models per person.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=uCfTxyEH3hf1k3~W4KdoaGaeASEATKnHARbzxRWlL04MvvQ-yN4k~GKXpV46~zBAJH2Kun6-hCgIgw78T5HuCJTpbuMNqqKmVMiIm8roNyxicSuAcYUfcK4MOkmLgo3zLxYxSO7zqRnqo0F2ein6ApMVOQry2o2-oq5RPmJbUPpCRorAAGfqHUt3BqpCCpyBo07BgPYrnGmqyS8VmSiXDdPnxxkHmN8JY4oB~xVd9eboRGcOnGFTCennCOpFWww1~6P6CYkHzMIqh~o2~ffIw~yQg6NIJb8Feun6cv16BLi7V13K~qV9zsVmIx3mMEFeRJFsU-R5XOuxrugx5Z-qOg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Number of models generated over time in days since the launch of SpaghettiLens; the black line shows all models, and the coloured lines show the five most active candidates. A total of 377 models were generated for 58 lens candidates, eight users contributed more than five models per person.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig1.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/106685831/stx3012fig1.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig1.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"106685831\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/stx3012fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&Signature=fIx9JxpOjLGmqdYACWj~PHQpZOHInZOTK3DwggR8xecqajXHu4Xi0yqlKHGg4ir6X3lehoLtkHiL4x34uXgaMp6kaJoepACHSrYvQUaF-bDlmn24uzJc0Nfab0cCuugojUjCBu6xWhfXuAOfHbkSPjxFGLpEWF9FEwLiKxphwhYt9fv9lrD0n8VHsQwUFpiNOgU6deUl9AXdnNGRNbo1m99BBZ~NBaWbI1szcbSSg3ythPjDGfUQbCdIxII3ed3cVAg0I2IwvyhJ2fRpsMv5hJrjInY8Ivwl7mkDtiPtVQUBqW~rQ5GPjrmWr9cfoQYDgwdUzFVgE9rIdTmDKpPvlA__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=106685831&ar=4655189&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig1.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Number of models generated over time in days since the launch of SpaghettiLens; the black line shows all models, and the coloured lines show the five most active candidates. A total of 377 models were generated for 58 lens candidates, eight users contributed more than five models per person.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">In parallel, K\u00fcng et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) tested the system on simulated lenses and identified some areas for improvement. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec7-1\"></span><a href=\"#sec7-1\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">A1</a>, we introduce fitting of the surface brightness profile of the source. This feature has not been included yet in SpaghettiLens, but we carried the analysis during post-processing for a few interesting cases. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec7-2\"></span><a href=\"#sec7-2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">A2</a>, we show that fine-grained mass maps within the central region relieve a tendency in the earlier work for mass profiles to be too shallow. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec7-3\"></span><a href=\"#sec7-3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">A3</a>, we consider the possibility of fitting a parametric lens model to the ensemble.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We characterize each model with seven diagnostics, grouped into three categories, whose purpose is to help identify the most likely cases of a gravitational lens, as well as flag the most interesting candidates for future follow-up observations. The diagnostics are as follows. <ul class=\"roman-lower\"><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">First, we have diagnostics based on morphology. Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a> and Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> explain this diagnostic in more detail. We consider: <ul class=\"list-simple\"><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">(a) Whether the images are unblended: Distinct, unblended images are an advantage in modelling, although not essential.</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">(b) Whether all images are discernible. The topography of an arrival-time surface, as encoded by a spaghetti diagram, may require more images than are visible, in which case the modeller has to insert conjectural image positions.</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">(c) Whether the lens is isolated.</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">(d) The image morphology concisely described: double or quads, further sub-categorized to indicate the elongation direction of the lensing mass.</p></li></ul></p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">Secondly, we have mass models, covered in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>. We assess the following points: <ul class=\"list-simple\"><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">(e) Whether the mass map is reasonable (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a>).</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">(f) Whether the arrival-time surface and synthetic image are plausible. In particular, an unsatisfactory model is flagged when additional images are implied in regions where they are not observed (see Figs\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>,\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> and\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>).</p></li></ul></p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">Thirdly, whether the total implied lensing mass determined from the lens model is plausible, given the photometry of the lensing galaxy. In this work, we define the lensing mass as the sum of all mass tiles in the model. These mass tiles reach out to typically twice the radius of the outermost image. Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a> explains how we compare the lensing mass with the stellar mass. Galaxies may have haloes extending well beyond the mass maps in the models, so the calculated lensing mass is only a lower bound on the total galaxy mass. Hence, the lensing mass should be somewhere between the stellar mass (lower bound) and the total halo mass (upper bound). Extrapolation of the lens model to estimate the full virial mass may be possible (cf. Leier et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), but is not attempted in this work. <ul class=\"list-simple\"><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">(g) We then introduce a so-called halo index (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$\\mathcal {H}$|\u2060</span>), which quantifies how the lensing mass compares with these two constraints (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig7\" data-open=\"fig7\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">7</a>).</p></li></ul></p></li></ul></p>                        <a id=\"106685834\" scrollto-destination=\"106685834\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=JLxDGzZllpFMvjk3d29aIWe5EK1SzaqSRtdiMSepJybDVTWJPV7EOqgfXEUr2Ai6OUr3JBwu3Jq2S0vhabQADGhtWVDbu4~WUfNiJPWm~vYDAyVNKfHeXur7zSco5gad5Bt7hBC54zIdb75zb05j9fNfUNEjYCh66n9rmdcU0rtab2CqiVLxprjh9NvZXNyZAF0UWbsd9iza1DIJp1eBObUiIowRYSiMgRm-vcmsewKr2O-Gv0wYUpMQ-k3MfYeo9v9wubPugqvYW3DFA75IkuWgn5-NYykyh232FR1wpMl2WQfLenHXVmnyKmklC~5jr3zxj4RyLtslQeDw9agPmg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Nine of the lens candidates marked up with spaghetti diagrams. The reconstructed lensed features keep the Space Warps false-colour scheme from Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. The rest has been changed to black and white.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=106685837 id=\"106685837\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 IMAGE MORPHOLOGY</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The main input of a modeller to the process is a markup of the candidate lens system, which we call a spaghetti diagram. This is a sketch of the arrival-time surface from a point-like source, with proposed locations of maxima, minima and saddle points, and an implied time-ordering of the images. Such information encodes a starting proposal for the mass distribution. A spaghetti diagram is thus a completely abstract construction, and moreover it refers to a simplified system with a point source. However, spaghetti diagrams are intuitive because they tend to resemble the form of lensed arcs (see fig. 3 of Ferreras, Saha &amp; Burles\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>), and of course they are simple to draw, and easy to vary and refine in an open collaborative environment. This makes them very practical for non-professional lens enthusiasts in the citizen\u2013science community. Details and tests are given in K\u00fcng et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We now discuss the diagnostics that can be taken from the process of drawing the spaghetti diagram, even before detailed mass-modelling takes place. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> shows nine examples, each consisting of a cut-out of the Space\u2009Warps image of a lens candidate, marked up with a spaghetti diagram. The volunteers are initially presented a square image with side 82\u2009arcsec (440\u2009pixels) in full size, but they have the ability to zoom in individually. The cut-outs presented in Figs\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>\u2013<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a> are rescaled during post-processing, relative to the outermost image.</p>                        <a id=\"106685840\" scrollto-destination=\"106685840\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=XGA8KgVsAa3cUYYi246bl9q~MQSc6yIJ1DXYbGLgQWZFLagF9Bvzjums-7Q8Cll3g1e0Wh0OcSoFwEQsNeqoskhT4703tJKBriPoiOC3-CFYrigcciaKF-Olkp8vg3LRNZV0gIt6fQikW00-~3OTeS3H-ooqKw09HmJLQ8C~fq4qQIo6YWK1fw9FtAb20U1VrMk4U0wyO~PUSIyuDRp4lQoj6djZFdG0d3Q3p-K1BYo6R43B1~RY-VzY-E7GCB5l6rn4SsSyIRrIDTAr9HIAphHPT1L18vih5~9uVTD5pM5g1aOOLz7EMdI0o9bF8ciNSKP81ahJgiHB6PxL8LNtDg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Ensemble-average mass distribution \u03ba for which the results Figs\u00a03\u20134 were derived. The dashed curves denote \u03ba\u00a0=\u00a01. Most of the mass maps have a 180\u00b0-rotation symmetry, which is imposed by default. For SW\u200902 and SW\u200957, where the lensing mass is clearly asymmetric, the modeller chose to turn off the symmetry.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig5.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/106685840/stx3012fig5.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig5.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"106685840\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/stx3012fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&Signature=LOUFOuxyg77ts10JZbiFIdpWGhqcfqx2FByG~14EM-JmiHR6xEpyOBUwj2g6EqVwnqeOHfuy3BqbS-PEdPosxlTJTsSZXupGplgItDHDMh4jXV2JokPVJ46yHzeaO1~-jviLtYO2HSabxsX79vME~VfKjblf~sNVJl1f00sfwMqjz1Q6-W68R~2pZ5AII5xU6kYHEsGCZ4NeN~6Xn-ulJ08jXxvkFIvoy923RJ0QjpkHRCGsYH5U-sWB1JdOCZIxUs~sviJOy5l9r1qq-RbzdjnAwGnbPNO9V8HL9ss2ZUesobPco5j6-Z0gxxahaqbyREfgONh2S2xbqcjWsNPWKg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=106685840&ar=4655189&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig5.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Ensemble-average mass distribution \u03ba for which the results Figs\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>\u2013<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> were derived. For SW\u200902 and SW\u200957, where the lensing mass is clearly asymmetric, the modeller chose to turn off the symmetry.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=XGA8KgVsAa3cUYYi246bl9q~MQSc6yIJ1DXYbGLgQWZFLagF9Bvzjums-7Q8Cll3g1e0Wh0OcSoFwEQsNeqoskhT4703tJKBriPoiOC3-CFYrigcciaKF-Olkp8vg3LRNZV0gIt6fQikW00-~3OTeS3H-ooqKw09HmJLQ8C~fq4qQIo6YWK1fw9FtAb20U1VrMk4U0wyO~PUSIyuDRp4lQoj6djZFdG0d3Q3p-K1BYo6R43B1~RY-VzY-E7GCB5l6rn4SsSyIRrIDTAr9HIAphHPT1L18vih5~9uVTD5pM5g1aOOLz7EMdI0o9bF8ciNSKP81ahJgiHB6PxL8LNtDg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Ensemble-average mass distribution \u03ba for which the results Figs\u00a03\u20134 were derived. The dashed curves denote \u03ba\u00a0=\u00a01. Most of the mass maps have a 180\u00b0-rotation symmetry, which is imposed by default. For SW\u200902 and SW\u200957, where the lensing mass is clearly asymmetric, the modeller chose to turn off the symmetry.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig5.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/106685840/stx3012fig5.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig5.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"106685840\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/stx3012fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&Signature=LOUFOuxyg77ts10JZbiFIdpWGhqcfqx2FByG~14EM-JmiHR6xEpyOBUwj2g6EqVwnqeOHfuy3BqbS-PEdPosxlTJTsSZXupGplgItDHDMh4jXV2JokPVJ46yHzeaO1~-jviLtYO2HSabxsX79vME~VfKjblf~sNVJl1f00sfwMqjz1Q6-W68R~2pZ5AII5xU6kYHEsGCZ4NeN~6Xn-ulJ08jXxvkFIvoy923RJ0QjpkHRCGsYH5U-sWB1JdOCZIxUs~sviJOy5l9r1qq-RbzdjnAwGnbPNO9V8HL9ss2ZUesobPco5j6-Z0gxxahaqbyREfgONh2S2xbqcjWsNPWKg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=106685840&ar=4655189&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig5.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Ensemble-average mass distribution \u03ba for which the results Figs\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>\u2013<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> were derived. The dashed curves denote \u03ba\u00a0=\u00a01. Most of the mass maps have a 180\u00b0-rotation symmetry, which is imposed by default. For SW\u200902 and SW\u200957, where the lensing mass is clearly asymmetric, the modeller chose to turn off the symmetry.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">All the examples shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> identify five locations: the centre of the main lensing galaxy, which is also a maximum of the arrival-time surface (red dots); two minima (blue dots); and two saddle points (green dots and also self-intersections of the curves). Only two (SW\u200905 and SW\u200942) of the nine systems, however, have five distinct features in plausible locations. In the other seven examples, an arc is interpreted as a blend of three or four images. This defines the \u2018unblended images\u2019 diagnostic. Note that this characterization could be different if the spaghetti diagram were different. For example, SW\u200928 has also been modelled with the arc on the right interpreted as a single image, rather than as three images as shown in the figure; for such a model, the \u2018unblended images\u2019 diagnostic would be true.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The second diagnostic checks whether all images are visible. For example, we see in SW\u200958 at the top left of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> that an image at the second minimum is conjectural and does not correspond to any visible feature.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The third diagnostic tests whether the lens is isolated, or whether other galaxies could contribute to the lensing, based on visual inspection of the field. For this, we do not consider stars or other clearly foreground objects. Additional galaxies contributing to the lensing mass can be marked by the volunteer alongside the spaghetti diagrams. An example can be seen as the grey dot and circle in the cut-out with SW\u200957 at the top right of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. Objects marked in this way are modelled as point masses. Other possible contributors to lensing are galaxies or groups that are not in the immediate vicinity of the lensed images, yet massive enough to exert an influence. These are accounted for by allowing a constant but adjustable external shear.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We remark that the lack of expected lensed images, or the presence of blended images or perturbing galaxies, does not imply that a given candidate is unlikely to be a lens. This means, rather, that the models are more uncertain and perhaps could be more easily improved by trying further variations in the markup.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The fourth diagnostic is based on the fact that the arrangement of lensed images of a point-like source through non-circular gravitational lens depends on the location of the source relative to the long and short axes of the lens. This dependence is quite robust and independent of many other details of the lensing mass distribution. Sources close to being dead-centre behind a lens tend to produce quads; sources at larger transverse distance tend to produce doubles. We denote these as Q and D, respectively, and add a prefix to the Q systems as follows: we write LQ if the source is inferred as displaced along the long axis of the lens, SQ if displaced along the short axis, IQ if inclined to both axes, and CQ if only very little or no displacement is evident. Although the unlensed source and its location are obviously not seen, the LQ, SQ, IQ and CQ cases correspond to easily seen image morphologies (see e.g. Saha &amp; Williams\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>). <ul class=\"roman-lower\"><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">The simplest is the LQ case: this creates a saddle point and two minima in an arc, with the second saddle point on the other side of the lensing galaxy, closer to the galaxy than the arc. SW\u200958 and SW\u200928 in the upper row of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> are typical examples of LQ. If the source were moved outwards along the short axis, the minimum-saddle-minimum set would merge into a single minimum, leaving a D system; the transition is known as a cusp catastrophe.</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">The middle row of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> shows three IQ systems: SW\u200905, SW\u200942 and SW\u200919. This type has a characteristic asymmetry, often with two images close together. If the source were moved outwards, the minimum-saddle pair would merge and mutually cancel, leaving again a D system. This transition is known as a fold catastrophe.</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">The lower row of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> shows three SQ systems: SW\u200909, SW\u200929 and SW\u200902. The failed model, SW\u200957, at top right may also belong to this category. Here, the images have a fairly symmetric arrangement with an arc and a counter-image on the other side, but the spaghetti diagram is completely asymmetric. If the source were moved outwards along the long axis, the saddle-minimum-saddle set would merge into a single saddle \u2013 another form of cusp catastrophe. SQ can be visually distinguished from LQ by the relative distances of the arc and the counter-image. For SQ, the arc is closer, and for LQ the counter-image is closer.</p></li></ul></p><p class=\"chapter-para\">CQ systems are often called \u2018cross\u2019 or \u2018Einstein-cross\u2019 systems; IQ systems are sometimes called \u2018folds\u2019, with \u2018cusp\u2019 commonly used for both SQ and LQ. The labels \u2018short-axis quad\u2019 and so on are not standard in the literature, but the morphological classification they express is familiar to experienced modellers. Hence, they can be useful to researchers wishing to apply other modelling methods to the same systems.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=106685847 id=\"106685847\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 MASS MODELS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Once a spaghetti diagram has been drawn on a web browser, it is forwarded to a server-side numerical framework, which searches for mass maps consistent with the image locations, parities and time ordering, given by the modeller. The mass maps are made up of mass tiles and are free-form, but are required to be concentrated around the identified lens centre (see Coles, Read &amp; Saha\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>, for the precise formulation of the search problem). The modeller can also set various options for the search, such as the number of mass tiles and the extent of the mass map; all options have defaults. Typically, there are \u223c500 mass tiles arranged in a disc, centred on the lensing galaxy and extending to twice the radius of the outermost image. By default, the mass distributed is required to have a 180\u00b0-rotation symmetry, but this option can be unset. Assuming mass distributions can be found, which in practice is usually the case, a statistical ensemble of 200 two-dimensional mass maps is returned. From each mass map, further quantities such as lens potentials or enclosed masses can be derived. Thus, there are ensembles of 200 values for the surface density at any point, for the enclosed mass within a given radius and so on. In this paper, we present the averages and ranges of different quantities, but other quantities such as 90\u2009per\u2009cent confidence ranges could also be computed. The whole ensemble of mass maps, along with derived quantities and uncertainties, makes up one SpaghettiLens model.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The mass will naturally depend on the lens and source redshifts, which are unknown when a lens candidate is first identified. However, this is not a problem, because a model can be trivially rescaled to use better redshift values, as they become available. The mass normalization of the models is proportional, through the angular critical density, to the factor <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$d_L{\\, } d_S{\\, } d_{LS}^{-1}$|\u2060</span>, where <em>d<sub>L</sub></em>, <em>d<sub>S</sub></em> and <em>d<sub>LS</sub></em> are the usual angular-diameter distances. In the redshift ranges typical of galaxy lensing, the normalization factor is roughly proportional to the lens redshift, and weakly dependent on the source redshift. This work applies photometric redshifts from the CFHTLS pipeline (Coupon et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>) to the candidate lensing galaxies; the values range from <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.2 to 1 (see Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>). The source redshifts are assumed as <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02, unless an unambiguous photometric redshift is available. The lens redshifts entail rather big uncertainties, up to a few tens of per cent (see fig. 5 in Coupon et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>). The lensing masses would be uncertain at the same level. On the other hand, the lensing masses in the sample range from 10<sup>11</sup> to 10<sup>13</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>; in comparison, the redshift uncertainty is not so important in this preliminary analysis.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The ensemble of mass maps can be post-processed in many different ways. Four different graphical quantities are particularly useful.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a> shows the arrival-time surfaces corresponding to the spaghetti diagrams of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. The arrival-time contours look like machine-made elaborations of the input spaghetti diagrams. If the saddle-point contours in the arrival time are qualitatively the same as the curves in the spaghetti diagram (the detailed shape of the spaghetti curves is unimportant), it immediately suggests a successful model. On the other hand, if the arrival-time surface has unexpected minima or saddle points, and especially if the unexpected features are far from identified lens images, that signals an improbable model. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> shows what we call synthetic images, meaning reconstructions of the extended lensed features by fitting for a source. These were generated by a new method, explained in Appendix\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec7-1\"></span><a href=\"#sec7-1\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">A1</a>, implemented during the offline post-processing after the modelling process was complete. The synthetic images provided by SpaghettiLens during the collaborative modelling and discussion were more crude; those are included in the <span class=\"content-section supplementary-material\"><a path-from-xml=\"sup1\" href=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/stx3012_supp.zip?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=UiNzDmc6Ie7tX7zJPV4HozVXgKiPPJ3QRZVNcHiwP1gM3AVHcnF2KJKe78hQ4gNPw0O8Uwxc4uTlonczNekq994i9yM80hBlYEFO9Rq11vw9ohV9jJgQaYCu5DXpZFKpBWx9jNgLZC~bVGc-KtPgC1IQ5OahMgw5drFuqzT0wLU7z5zLXZND7Tf34MGcu4YdMyYIvnCrm2fAgYqIEaiDUavJ23Se1YO7xYwbJp2deU0YqF7gEOAgncZWfhQqq5iVWINuJXHI8Ianu6qtXsDUUdD2sziQWjwVUjE7X1mFfXfIvLHSayyhrwe551USLF8B955Mk~Nxmxn4Gt4ouv~gzQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\">online supplement</a></span>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The arrival-time surface and synthetic image are summarized by one diagnostic, the most important of all: are the lensed features satisfactorily reproduced? This diagnostic remains a judgment call by modellers. A useful quantitative criterion for whether the synthetic image is consistent with the data would need to allow for PSF dependence and unmodelled substructure \u2013 otherwise all models would be summarily rejected, something left for a future implementation in SpaghettiLens.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a> shows the projected mass maps of the sample. In fact, this figure only shows the ensemble-average mass maps, and not the variation within the ensemble, from which uncertainties can be inferred. The same applies to the arrival-time surfaces and synthetic images in the previous two figures. The uncertainties will be shown in a concise form in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a> makes evident the tiled nature of the mass model. The tiles can be smoothed over by interpolation, and this was done in the mass maps during the modelling process, available in the online version. It is interesting, however, to note the tiling artefacts, if only as a reminder that the substructure in the mass distribution is very uncertain, even if some integrated quantities are well constrained. How the free-form mass maps relate to parametrized lens models is discussed in Appendix\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec7-3\"></span><a href=\"#sec7-3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">A3</a>. Note that although the mass distribution can have discontinuous jumps, the lens equation and arrival-time surface are continuous.</p>                        <a id=\"106685854\" scrollto-destination=\"106685854\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig6\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 6.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012fig6.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=Dzs0ayZ4DQ1cAiGDfwUYklj1IeFGQquSmOC9GAZM~jnYJtuPO32JVMdvX2b7IoV26sM~~bRHftGPo0OiSl0dPZ~b2KACG71BMImfPAOaQVUUsXJ4iKESPHiU2JAmiZVxrdV6WBUe8qDbES~dErnE4ycycctD1bIIn6Q3h7llwdA6OFRq1hrml6WvSK0BClulz1GdCYmY9lm2AsvtU3mbOpPwZQahUqIfTLCJA7Bh0r-Q5jKi85XDku9zkh5tMUjO-xVZADVx2tAcQcUfPWnts~Q9akUE2mSSBezv9MepBc8ej~Zs2wqaFhBD6N8TG-HGhbnAGuHvJAjmkl7CxVNdoQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Cumulative circular averages of the mass maps from Fig.\u00a05, with uncertainties. More precisely, we show the enclosed mass within a given projected radius, expressed as the mean \u03ba with a given number of arcsec from the centre of the lensing galaxy. The orange bands refer to the full ensemble of mass maps for the models, while the red curves show the ensemble averages. The dashed vertical line indicates the notional Einstein radius, or where the mean enclosed \u03ba is unity. The short vertical arrows mark the positions of the images (maxima, saddle points and minima).</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a> shows the enclosed-mass profiles, expressed as the average convergence, \u03ba, within circles of a given projected radius. Uncertainties are included (see the figure caption for details). Appendix <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec7-2\"></span><a href=\"#sec7-2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">A2</a> describes the improvements made since our earlier work (K\u00fcng et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), to allow for steeper profiles in the inner regions. The enclosed mass is typically best constrained at the notional Einstein radius, becoming more uncertain at larger and smaller radii.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The mass maps and mass profiles are the basis of a further diagnostic: are the mass distributions plausible? This is also a judgment call made by modellers, but it showed to be a powerful diagnostic, summarizing three aspects. The overall shape is forced to be 180\u00b0-rotation symmetric, usually a plausible assumption, but volunteers can deactivate this constraint. The profile slope turned out to be a good indicator of plausible models, as can seen by contrasting the model for SW\u200957 with the rest of the sample: The missing core in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a> and the flat profile in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a> disqualify this model. The clumpiness of the mass map is another useful indicator. Flat profile slopes can often be identified directly in the mass map, where the mass tiles form a checkerboard pattern.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">More experienced volunteers applied these diagnostics already during the process of creating models as a criteria of a successful model, the evaluation presented in this work however was generated by the authors during post-processing.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=106685858 id=\"106685858\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 STELLAR AND HALO MASS ESTIMATES</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The stellar masses of the lens galaxies are derived by a comparison of the photometric data with stellar <em>M</em>/<em>L</em> estimates from population synthesis models. In principle, a detailed analysis of the spectral energy distribution is needed to derive accurate stellar masses (e.g. Gallazzi &amp; Bell\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>; Taylor et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). However, at the redshifts probed, the photometric data mainly constrain the information-rich 4000\u2009\u00c5 break region, whose strength depends sensitively on age and metallicity, thereby providing a strong constraint on the stellar <em>M</em>/<em>L</em>. Hence, estimates to within \u223c0.3\u2009dex in log\u2009(<em>M</em><sub>stel</sub>/M<sub>\u2299</sub>) can be derived with a single colour, preferably tracing a rest-frame colour similar to <em>U</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>V</em> (see fig. 1 of Ferreras et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>), assuming a universal initial mass function (IMF). There is evidence from detailed absorption line strength analysis that massive galaxies can feature a non-standard IMF (e.g. Ferreras et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>). However, these variations, towards a bottom-heavy distribution, are typically found in the cores of massive early-type galaxies (La Barbera et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). The effect of these variations on the stellar <em>M</em>/<em>L</em> of lensing systems is still rather controversial (Smith, Lucey &amp; Conroy\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib37\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib37\" data-open=\"bib37\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Leier et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In this paper, we further simplify the analysis by assuming a relationship between the apparent total magnitude and stellar mass, at the redshift of the lens. For typical stellar-population parameters, the variation of this relation is at most \u0394 log\u2009M<sub><em>s</em></sub> \u223c 1\u2009dex. A further potential systematic can arise from contamination of the light of the lensing galaxy by the lensed background source. Reducing or eliminating the latter would require detailed fitting of light distributions for each candidate (see Leier et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>), which we have not yet attempted. Nonetheless, because the lensing masses range over two orders of magnitude, it is still interesting to compare them with rough estimates of stellar mass.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We make use of the Bruzual &amp; Charlot (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>) models to derive two functional forms of the stellar mass with respect to the <em>i</em>\u0384-band magnitudes. The models have solar metallicity, with a Chabrier IMF, and assume two different age trends: a \u2018young\u2019 model, with a constant 500\u2009Myr age at all redshifts, and an \u2018old\u2019 model where the age is the oldest one possible at each redshift, adopting a standard \u039bCDM model with <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a070\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>\u2009Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup> and \u03a9<sub><em>m</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.3.</p><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig7\" data-open=\"fig7\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">7</a> shows a comparison of stellar and lensing mass in our sample. The comparatively large span of the error bars in stellar mass (horizontal axis) shows the range between the masses derived using the two age trends, respectively, and lies between 0.4 and 0.8\u2009dex. It will be improved in future work by the use of available optical and NIR magnitudes to derive more accurate constraints on the stellar populations. In addition, we also derive halo masses for the lenses using an abundance-matching formula. This technique matches the distribution function of observed stellar mass in galaxies with that of dark-halo masses from <em>N</em>-body simulations, to define a simple relation between stellar mass and halo mass. We emphasize that a halo mass from abundance matching should be considered an \u2018average\u2019 estimate, and a significant scatter can be expected as galaxies with the same stellar mass can be found in different environments. We refer the reader to Leier et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) for an assessment of the effect of abundance matching on the derivation of dark matter halo properties in lensing galaxies. We follow the prescription of Moster et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>), namely: <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ1\" content-id=\"equ1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\frac{M_{\\rm stel}}{M_{\\rm halo}} = \\frac{2C_0}{(M_{\\rm halo}/M_1)^{-\\beta } + (M_{\\rm halo}/M_1)^\\gamma }\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(1)</span></div><div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"\" content-id=\"\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray*}\r\nC_0 &amp;=&amp; 0.02820, M_1 = 10^{11.884} {\\, }\\mathrm{M}_{\\odot } \\nonumber\\\\\r\n\\beta &amp;=&amp; 1.057, \\gamma = 0.556.\r\n\\end{eqnarray*} </div></div></div>Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig7\" data-open=\"fig7\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">7</a> may be compared with Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> in More et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). The comparison of lensing and stellar mass produces the last of our model diagnostics, defined as a halo-matching index: <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ2\" content-id=\"equ2\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\mathcal {H}\\equiv \\frac{\\ln (M/M_{\\rm stel})}{\\ln (M_{\\rm halo}/M_{\\rm stel})}\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(2)</span></div>that relates the observed lensing to stellar mass, with the global ratio expected if the host halo corresponds to the average value derived by abundance matching. Several cases for <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mathcal {H}$|</span> can be considered: <ul class=\"roman-lower\"><li><p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mathcal {H}&lt; 0$|</span> is unphysical because <em>M</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>M</em><sub>stel</sub>.</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mathcal {H}= 0$|</span> means the stellar mass exactly accounts for the lensing mass (i.e. no dark matter affects the lensing model).</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$0 &lt; \\mathcal {H}&lt; 1$|</span> is the typical situation, where the lens includes stars and dark matter, but not the full halo.</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mathcal {H}= 1$|</span> means that the lens consists of the entire halo.</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mathcal {H}&gt; 1$|</span> is in tension with abundance matching, because the lensing mass exceeds the expected halo mass.</p></li></ul></div>                        <a id=\"106685863\" scrollto-destination=\"106685863\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig7\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 7.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012fig7.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=03YPji~B-f7wgiy7tGSumUmH9Bk8Ox1nzIw2W34AbfSV8sE7X4W~EmgfqHnzciPIIq4izj3thJQkq7BoFhEBS-kMuN8ItRIFFnULENyHa0jmnl3TQInwLOaZCjpiI1tCzfyoa9fgG5r8gTizXN7LuS2NMf49WGMEIdJAs~id3lT~xPRbXr4F5mPMMPSKOU9TDDlZfaBpY3S0-kJXEZ1ZwbgKOKaaSiAvd6d4~QGxicTBQjw5Ey6V55Yj3ZpPIiu-vlV9yYhOKNe6SDESVSmuM4aDLRDVfuctNF-88I5-PBuVDlOi4heIYDYkCFQWEuUcjS6ni19U4PWi-dghQlWGxw__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Total mass in the model against the estimated stellar mass, alongside the values for the whole sample. (The labelled orange bars are the systems shown in detail in Figs\u00a02\u20136.) The horizontal extent of each bar indicates the extreme cases of a young (0.5\u00a0Gyr-old) stellar population and the oldest possible population at the given redshift. The vertical extent indicates the spread of masses in the lens-model ensemble. The lower-right shaded region is unphysical according to the stellar-population models, because it gives M\u00a0&lt;\u00a0Mstel. The upper-left shaded region is unphysical according to abundance matching (see Section\u00a05) because it gives M\u00a0&gt;\u00a0Mhalo. That is to say, the unshaded region is $0&lt;\\mathcal {H}&lt;1$.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig7.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/106685863/stx3012fig7.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig7.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"106685863\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/stx3012fig7.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&Signature=kgTEd0WCtDT5YukNVpHTRpy~47z1YvyNE6Lt8sEek4sGBnWeRU8ji6SGx2QMvQYXCmX1d1iGTWGo8qD1CNZN9t~K7yOFm5ha1z3MvNAlfCxVPSmVqi13QOVZty-d0SIXihLCkhS0pkA~CHelDWSYpaig~wdmBK75Fbg1hLY5-XCu4Fx2MkiCWAUn58XXvKH2xXrnYIuj3r2~fxXhtfkcwEdxNP7y41Y0UmoLIfEUD2GqTyTSALXFD1y2teB1EMRP7fRXy1FdLvDR6iRiwUUswNNPchGkRQWuLlqv67AC4UfbF8qN9RpiRKMdECaRCqS7~LXq9mqcmspzTZmdU0BW6A__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=106685863&ar=4655189&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig7.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Total mass in the model against the estimated stellar mass, alongside the values for the whole sample. (The labelled orange bars are the systems shown in detail in Figs\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>\u2013<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>.) That is to say, the unshaded region is <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$0&lt;\\mathcal {H}&lt;1$|\u2060</span>.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig7\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 7.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012fig7.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=03YPji~B-f7wgiy7tGSumUmH9Bk8Ox1nzIw2W34AbfSV8sE7X4W~EmgfqHnzciPIIq4izj3thJQkq7BoFhEBS-kMuN8ItRIFFnULENyHa0jmnl3TQInwLOaZCjpiI1tCzfyoa9fgG5r8gTizXN7LuS2NMf49WGMEIdJAs~id3lT~xPRbXr4F5mPMMPSKOU9TDDlZfaBpY3S0-kJXEZ1ZwbgKOKaaSiAvd6d4~QGxicTBQjw5Ey6V55Yj3ZpPIiu-vlV9yYhOKNe6SDESVSmuM4aDLRDVfuctNF-88I5-PBuVDlOi4heIYDYkCFQWEuUcjS6ni19U4PWi-dghQlWGxw__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Total mass in the model against the estimated stellar mass, alongside the values for the whole sample.
