For SW\u200902 and SW\u200957, where the lensing mass is clearly asymmetric, the modeller chose to turn off the symmetry.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig5\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 5.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=XGA8KgVsAa3cUYYi246bl9q~MQSc6yIJ1DXYbGLgQWZFLagF9Bvzjums-7Q8Cll3g1e0Wh0OcSoFwEQsNeqoskhT4703tJKBriPoiOC3-CFYrigcciaKF-Olkp8vg3LRNZV0gIt6fQikW00-~3OTeS3H-ooqKw09HmJLQ8C~fq4qQIo6YWK1fw9FtAb20U1VrMk4U0wyO~PUSIyuDRp4lQoj6djZFdG0d3Q3p-K1BYo6R43B1~RY-VzY-E7GCB5l6rn4SsSyIRrIDTAr9HIAphHPT1L18vih5~9uVTD5pM5g1aOOLz7EMdI0o9bF8ciNSKP81ahJgiHB6PxL8LNtDg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Ensemble-average mass distribution \u03ba for which the results Figs\u00a03\u20134 were derived. The dashed curves denote \u03ba\u00a0=\u00a01. Most of the mass maps have a 180\u00b0-rotation symmetry, which is imposed by default. For SW\u200902 and SW\u200957, where the lensing mass is clearly asymmetric, the modeller chose to turn off the symmetry.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig5.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/106685840/stx3012fig5.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig5.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"106685840\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/stx3012fig5.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&Signature=LOUFOuxyg77ts10JZbiFIdpWGhqcfqx2FByG~14EM-JmiHR6xEpyOBUwj2g6EqVwnqeOHfuy3BqbS-PEdPosxlTJTsSZXupGplgItDHDMh4jXV2JokPVJ46yHzeaO1~-jviLtYO2HSabxsX79vME~VfKjblf~sNVJl1f00sfwMqjz1Q6-W68R~2pZ5AII5xU6kYHEsGCZ4NeN~6Xn-ulJ08jXxvkFIvoy923RJ0QjpkHRCGsYH5U-sWB1JdOCZIxUs~sviJOy5l9r1qq-RbzdjnAwGnbPNO9V8HL9ss2ZUesobPco5j6-Z0gxxahaqbyREfgONh2S2xbqcjWsNPWKg__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=106685840&ar=4655189&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig5.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Ensemble-average mass distribution \u03ba for which the results Figs\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a>\u2013<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> were derived. The dashed curves denote \u03ba\u00a0=\u00a01. Most of the mass maps have a 180\u00b0-rotation symmetry, which is imposed by default. For SW\u200902 and SW\u200957, where the lensing mass is clearly asymmetric, the modeller chose to turn off the symmetry.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">All the examples shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> identify five locations: the centre of the main lensing galaxy, which is also a maximum of the arrival-time surface (red dots); two minima (blue dots); and two saddle points (green dots and also self-intersections of the curves). Only two (SW\u200905 and SW\u200942) of the nine systems, however, have five distinct features in plausible locations. In the other seven examples, an arc is interpreted as a blend of three or four images. This defines the \u2018unblended images\u2019 diagnostic. Note that this characterization could be different if the spaghetti diagram were different. For example, SW\u200928 has also been modelled with the arc on the right interpreted as a single image, rather than as three images as shown in the figure; for such a model, the \u2018unblended images\u2019 diagnostic would be true.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The second diagnostic checks whether all images are visible. For example, we see in SW\u200958 at the top left of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> that an image at the second minimum is conjectural and does not correspond to any visible feature.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The third diagnostic tests whether the lens is isolated, or whether other galaxies could contribute to the lensing, based on visual inspection of the field. For this, we do not consider stars or other clearly foreground objects. Additional galaxies contributing to the lensing mass can be marked by the volunteer alongside the spaghetti diagrams. An example can be seen as the grey dot and circle in the cut-out with SW\u200957 at the top right of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. Objects marked in this way are modelled as point masses. Other possible contributors to lensing are galaxies or groups that are not in the immediate vicinity of the lensed images, yet massive enough to exert an influence. These are accounted for by allowing a constant but adjustable external shear.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We remark that the lack of expected lensed images, or the presence of blended images or perturbing galaxies, does not imply that a given candidate is unlikely to be a lens. This means, rather, that the models are more uncertain and perhaps could be more easily improved by trying further variations in the markup.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The fourth diagnostic is based on the fact that the arrangement of lensed images of a point-like source through non-circular gravitational lens depends on the location of the source relative to the long and short axes of the lens. This dependence is quite robust and independent of many other details of the lensing mass distribution. Sources close to being dead-centre behind a lens tend to produce quads; sources at larger transverse distance tend to produce doubles. We denote these as Q and D, respectively, and add a prefix to the Q systems as follows: we write LQ if the source is inferred as displaced along the long axis of the lens, SQ if displaced along the short axis, IQ if inclined to both axes, and CQ if only very little or no displacement is evident. Although the unlensed source and its location are obviously not seen, the LQ, SQ, IQ and CQ cases correspond to easily seen image morphologies (see e.g. Saha &amp; Williams\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>). <ul class=\"roman-lower\"><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">The simplest is the LQ case: this creates a saddle point and two minima in an arc, with the second saddle point on the other side of the lensing galaxy, closer to the galaxy than the arc. SW\u200958 and SW\u200928 in the upper row of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> are typical examples of LQ. If the source were moved outwards along the short axis, the minimum-saddle-minimum set would merge into a single minimum, leaving a D system; the transition is known as a cusp catastrophe.</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">The middle row of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> shows three IQ systems: SW\u200905, SW\u200942 and SW\u200919. This type has a characteristic asymmetry, often with two images close together. If the source were moved outwards, the minimum-saddle pair would merge and mutually cancel, leaving again a D system. This transition is known as a fold catastrophe.</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\">The lower row of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> shows three SQ systems: SW\u200909, SW\u200929 and SW\u200902. The failed model, SW\u200957, at top right may also belong to this category. Here, the images have a fairly symmetric arrangement with an arc and a counter-image on the other side, but the spaghetti diagram is completely asymmetric. If the source were moved outwards along the long axis, the saddle-minimum-saddle set would merge into a single saddle \u2013 another form of cusp catastrophe. SQ can be visually distinguished from LQ by the relative distances of the arc and the counter-image. For SQ, the arc is closer, and for LQ the counter-image is closer.</p></li></ul></p><p class=\"chapter-para\">CQ systems are often called \u2018cross\u2019 or \u2018Einstein-cross\u2019 systems; IQ systems are sometimes called \u2018folds\u2019, with \u2018cusp\u2019 commonly used for both SQ and LQ. The labels \u2018short-axis quad\u2019 and so on are not standard in the literature, but the morphological classification they express is familiar to experienced modellers. Hence, they can be useful to researchers wishing to apply other modelling methods to the same systems.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=106685847 id=\"106685847\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 MASS MODELS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Once a spaghetti diagram has been drawn on a web browser, it is forwarded to a server-side numerical framework, which searches for mass maps consistent with the image locations, parities and time ordering, given by the modeller. The mass maps are made up of mass tiles and are free-form, but are required to be concentrated around the identified lens centre (see Coles, Read &amp; Saha\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>, for the precise formulation of the search problem). The modeller can also set various options for the search, such as the number of mass tiles and the extent of the mass map; all options have defaults. Typically, there are \u223c500 mass tiles arranged in a disc, centred on the lensing galaxy and extending to twice the radius of the outermost image. By default, the mass distributed is required to have a 180\u00b0-rotation symmetry, but this option can be unset. Assuming mass distributions can be found, which in practice is usually the case, a statistical ensemble of 200 two-dimensional mass maps is returned. From each mass map, further quantities such as lens potentials or enclosed masses can be derived. Thus, there are ensembles of 200 values for the surface density at any point, for the enclosed mass within a given radius and so on. In this paper, we present the averages and ranges of different quantities, but other quantities such as 90\u2009per\u2009cent confidence ranges could also be computed. The whole ensemble of mass maps, along with derived quantities and uncertainties, makes up one SpaghettiLens model.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The mass will naturally depend on the lens and source redshifts, which are unknown when a lens candidate is first identified. However, this is not a problem, because a model can be trivially rescaled to use better redshift values, as they become available. The mass normalization of the models is proportional, through the angular critical density, to the factor <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$d_L{\\, } d_S{\\, } d_{LS}^{-1}$|\u2060</span>, where <em>d<sub>L</sub></em>, <em>d<sub>S</sub></em> and <em>d<sub>LS</sub></em> are the usual angular-diameter distances. In the redshift ranges typical of galaxy lensing, the normalization factor is roughly proportional to the lens redshift, and weakly dependent on the source redshift. This work applies photometric redshifts from the CFHTLS pipeline (Coupon et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>) to the candidate lensing galaxies; the values range from <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a00.2 to 1 (see Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>). The source redshifts are assumed as <em>z</em>\u00a0=\u00a02, unless an unambiguous photometric redshift is available. The lens redshifts entail rather big uncertainties, up to a few tens of per cent (see fig. 5 in Coupon et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>). The lensing masses would be uncertain at the same level. On the other hand, the lensing masses in the sample range from 10<sup>11</sup> to 10<sup>13</sup>\u2009M<sub>\u2299</sub>; in comparison, the redshift uncertainty is not so important in this preliminary analysis.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The ensemble of mass maps can be post-processed in many different ways. Four different graphical quantities are particularly useful.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig3\" data-open=\"fig3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">3</a> shows the arrival-time surfaces corresponding to the spaghetti diagrams of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>. The arrival-time contours look like machine-made elaborations of the input spaghetti diagrams. If the saddle-point contours in the arrival time are qualitatively the same as the curves in the spaghetti diagram (the detailed shape of the spaghetti curves is unimportant), it immediately suggests a successful model. On the other hand, if the arrival-time surface has unexpected minima or saddle points, and especially if the unexpected features are far from identified lens images, that signals an improbable model. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> shows what we call synthetic images, meaning reconstructions of the extended lensed features by fitting for a source. These were generated by a new method, explained in Appendix\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec7-1\"></span><a href=\"#sec7-1\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">A1</a>, implemented during the offline post-processing after the modelling process was complete. The synthetic images provided by SpaghettiLens during the collaborative modelling and discussion were more crude; those are included in the <span class=\"content-section supplementary-material\"><a path-from-xml=\"sup1\" href=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/stx3012_supp.zip?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=UiNzDmc6Ie7tX7zJPV4HozVXgKiPPJ3QRZVNcHiwP1gM3AVHcnF2KJKe78hQ4gNPw0O8Uwxc4uTlonczNekq994i9yM80hBlYEFO9Rq11vw9ohV9jJgQaYCu5DXpZFKpBWx9jNgLZC~bVGc-KtPgC1IQ5OahMgw5drFuqzT0wLU7z5zLXZND7Tf34MGcu4YdMyYIvnCrm2fAgYqIEaiDUavJ23Se1YO7xYwbJp2deU0YqF7gEOAgncZWfhQqq5iVWINuJXHI8Ianu6qtXsDUUdD2sziQWjwVUjE7X1mFfXfIvLHSayyhrwe551USLF8B955Mk~Nxmxn4Gt4ouv~gzQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\">online supplement</a></span>.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The arrival-time surface and synthetic image are summarized by one diagnostic, the most important of all: are the lensed features satisfactorily reproduced? This diagnostic remains a judgment call by modellers. A useful quantitative criterion for whether the synthetic image is consistent with the data would need to allow for PSF dependence and unmodelled substructure \u2013 otherwise all models would be summarily rejected, something left for a future implementation in SpaghettiLens.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a> shows the projected mass maps of the sample. In fact, this figure only shows the ensemble-average mass maps, and not the variation within the ensemble, from which uncertainties can be inferred. The same applies to the arrival-time surfaces and synthetic images in the previous two figures. The uncertainties will be shown in a concise form in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a> makes evident the tiled nature of the mass model. The tiles can be smoothed over by interpolation, and this was done in the mass maps during the modelling process, available in the online version. It is interesting, however, to note the tiling artefacts, if only as a reminder that the substructure in the mass distribution is very uncertain, even if some integrated quantities are well constrained. How the free-form mass maps relate to parametrized lens models is discussed in Appendix\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec7-3\"></span><a href=\"#sec7-3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">A3</a>. Note that although the mass distribution can have discontinuous jumps, the lens equation and arrival-time surface are continuous.</p>                        <a id=\"106685854\" scrollto-destination=\"106685854\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig6\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 6.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012fig6.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=Dzs0ayZ4DQ1cAiGDfwUYklj1IeFGQquSmOC9GAZM~jnYJtuPO32JVMdvX2b7IoV26sM~~bRHftGPo0OiSl0dPZ~b2KACG71BMImfPAOaQVUUsXJ4iKESPHiU2JAmiZVxrdV6WBUe8qDbES~dErnE4ycycctD1bIIn6Q3h7llwdA6OFRq1hrml6WvSK0BClulz1GdCYmY9lm2AsvtU3mbOpPwZQahUqIfTLCJA7Bh0r-Q5jKi85XDku9zkh5tMUjO-xVZADVx2tAcQcUfPWnts~Q9akUE2mSSBezv9MepBc8ej~Zs2wqaFhBD6N8TG-HGhbnAGuHvJAjmkl7CxVNdoQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Cumulative circular averages of the mass maps from Fig.\u00a05, with uncertainties. More precisely, we show the enclosed mass within a given projected radius, expressed as the mean \u03ba with a given number of arcsec from the centre of the lensing galaxy. The orange bands refer to the full ensemble of mass maps for the models, while the red curves show the ensemble averages. The dashed vertical line indicates the notional Einstein radius, or where the mean enclosed \u03ba is unity. The short vertical arrows mark the positions of the images (maxima, saddle points and minima).</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a> shows the enclosed-mass profiles, expressed as the average convergence, \u03ba, within circles of a given projected radius. Uncertainties are included (see the figure caption for details). Appendix <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec7-2\"></span><a href=\"#sec7-2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">A2</a> describes the improvements made since our earlier work (K\u00fcng et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), to allow for steeper profiles in the inner regions. The enclosed mass is typically best constrained at the notional Einstein radius, becoming more uncertain at larger and smaller radii.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The mass maps and mass profiles are the basis of a further diagnostic: are the mass distributions plausible? This is also a judgment call made by modellers, but it showed to be a powerful diagnostic, summarizing three aspects. The overall shape is forced to be 180\u00b0-rotation symmetric, usually a plausible assumption, but volunteers can deactivate this constraint. The profile slope turned out to be a good indicator of plausible models, as can seen by contrasting the model for SW\u200957 with the rest of the sample: The missing core in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig5\" data-open=\"fig5\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">5</a> and the flat profile in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a> disqualify this model. The clumpiness of the mass map is another useful indicator. Flat profile slopes can often be identified directly in the mass map, where the mass tiles form a checkerboard pattern.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">More experienced volunteers applied these diagnostics already during the process of creating models as a criteria of a successful model, the evaluation presented in this work however was generated by the authors during post-processing.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=106685858 id=\"106685858\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 STELLAR AND HALO MASS ESTIMATES</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The stellar masses of the lens galaxies are derived by a comparison of the photometric data with stellar <em>M</em>/<em>L</em> estimates from population synthesis models. In principle, a detailed analysis of the spectral energy distribution is needed to derive accurate stellar masses (e.g. Gallazzi &amp; Bell\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2009</a>; Taylor et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). However, at the redshifts probed, the photometric data mainly constrain the information-rich 4000\u2009\u00c5 break region, whose strength depends sensitively on age and metallicity, thereby providing a strong constraint on the stellar <em>M</em>/<em>L</em>. Hence, estimates to within \u223c0.3\u2009dex in log\u2009(<em>M</em><sub>stel</sub>/M<sub>\u2299</sub>) can be derived with a single colour, preferably tracing a rest-frame colour similar to <em>U</em>\u00a0\u2212\u00a0<em>V</em> (see fig. 1 of Ferreras et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>), assuming a universal initial mass function (IMF). There is evidence from detailed absorption line strength analysis that massive galaxies can feature a non-standard IMF (e.g. Ferreras et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>). However, these variations, towards a bottom-heavy distribution, are typically found in the cores of massive early-type galaxies (La Barbera et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). The effect of these variations on the stellar <em>M</em>/<em>L</em> of lensing systems is still rather controversial (Smith, Lucey &amp; Conroy\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib37\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib37\" data-open=\"bib37\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Leier et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In this paper, we further simplify the analysis by assuming a relationship between the apparent total magnitude and stellar mass, at the redshift of the lens. For typical stellar-population parameters, the variation of this relation is at most \u0394 log\u2009M<sub><em>s</em></sub> \u223c 1\u2009dex. A further potential systematic can arise from contamination of the light of the lensing galaxy by the lensed background source. Reducing or eliminating the latter would require detailed fitting of light distributions for each candidate (see Leier et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>), which we have not yet attempted. Nonetheless, because the lensing masses range over two orders of magnitude, it is still interesting to compare them with rough estimates of stellar mass.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We make use of the Bruzual &amp; Charlot (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2003</a>) models to derive two functional forms of the stellar mass with respect to the <em>i</em>\u0384-band magnitudes. The models have solar metallicity, with a Chabrier IMF, and assume two different age trends: a \u2018young\u2019 model, with a constant 500\u2009Myr age at all redshifts, and an \u2018old\u2019 model where the age is the oldest one possible at each redshift, adopting a standard \u039bCDM model with <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0=\u00a070\u2009km\u2009s<sup>\u22121</sup>\u2009Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup> and \u03a9<sub><em>m</em></sub>\u00a0=\u00a00.3.</p><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig7\" data-open=\"fig7\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">7</a> shows a comparison of stellar and lensing mass in our sample. The comparatively large span of the error bars in stellar mass (horizontal axis) shows the range between the masses derived using the two age trends, respectively, and lies between 0.4 and 0.8\u2009dex. It will be improved in future work by the use of available optical and NIR magnitudes to derive more accurate constraints on the stellar populations. In addition, we also derive halo masses for the lenses using an abundance-matching formula. This technique matches the distribution function of observed stellar mass in galaxies with that of dark-halo masses from <em>N</em>-body simulations, to define a simple relation between stellar mass and halo mass. We emphasize that a halo mass from abundance matching should be considered an \u2018average\u2019 estimate, and a significant scatter can be expected as galaxies with the same stellar mass can be found in different environments. We refer the reader to Leier et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) for an assessment of the effect of abundance matching on the derivation of dark matter halo properties in lensing galaxies. We follow the prescription of Moster et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>), namely: <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ1\" content-id=\"equ1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\frac{M_{\\rm stel}}{M_{\\rm halo}} = \\frac{2C_0}{(M_{\\rm halo}/M_1)^{-\\beta } + (M_{\\rm halo}/M_1)^\\gamma }\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(1)</span></div><div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"\" content-id=\"\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray*}\r\nC_0 &amp;=&amp; 0.02820, M_1 = 10^{11.884} {\\, }\\mathrm{M}_{\\odot } \\nonumber\\\\\r\n\\beta &amp;=&amp; 1.057, \\gamma = 0.556.\r\n\\end{eqnarray*} </div></div></div>Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig7\" data-open=\"fig7\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">7</a> may be compared with Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig4\" data-open=\"fig4\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">4</a> in More et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>). The comparison of lensing and stellar mass produces the last of our model diagnostics, defined as a halo-matching index: <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ2\" content-id=\"equ2\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\mathcal {H}\\equiv \\frac{\\ln (M/M_{\\rm stel})}{\\ln (M_{\\rm halo}/M_{\\rm stel})}\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(2)</span></div>that relates the observed lensing to stellar mass, with the global ratio expected if the host halo corresponds to the average value derived by abundance matching. Several cases for <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mathcal {H}$|</span> can be considered: <ul class=\"roman-lower\"><li><p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mathcal {H}&lt; 0$|</span> is unphysical because <em>M</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>M</em><sub>stel</sub>.</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mathcal {H}= 0$|</span> means the stellar mass exactly accounts for the lensing mass (i.e. no dark matter affects the lensing model).</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$0 &lt; \\mathcal {H}&lt; 1$|</span> is the typical situation, where the lens includes stars and dark matter, but not the full halo.</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mathcal {H}= 1$|</span> means that the lens consists of the entire halo.</p></li><li><p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mathcal {H}&gt; 1$|</span> is in tension with abundance matching, because the lensing mass exceeds the expected halo mass.</p></li></ul></div>                        <a id=\"106685863\" scrollto-destination=\"106685863\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig7\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 7.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012fig7.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=03YPji~B-f7wgiy7tGSumUmH9Bk8Ox1nzIw2W34AbfSV8sE7X4W~EmgfqHnzciPIIq4izj3thJQkq7BoFhEBS-kMuN8ItRIFFnULENyHa0jmnl3TQInwLOaZCjpiI1tCzfyoa9fgG5r8gTizXN7LuS2NMf49WGMEIdJAs~id3lT~xPRbXr4F5mPMMPSKOU9TDDlZfaBpY3S0-kJXEZ1ZwbgKOKaaSiAvd6d4~QGxicTBQjw5Ey6V55Yj3ZpPIiu-vlV9yYhOKNe6SDESVSmuM4aDLRDVfuctNF-88I5-PBuVDlOi4heIYDYkCFQWEuUcjS6ni19U4PWi-dghQlWGxw__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Total mass in the model against the estimated stellar mass, alongside the values for the whole sample. (The labelled orange bars are the systems shown in detail in Figs\u00a02\u20136.) The horizontal extent of each bar indicates the extreme cases of a young (0.5\u00a0Gyr-old) stellar population and the oldest possible population at the given redshift. The vertical extent indicates the spread of masses in the lens-model ensemble. The lower-right shaded region is unphysical according to the stellar-population models, because it gives M\u00a0&lt;\u00a0Mstel. The upper-left shaded region is unphysical according to abundance matching (see Section\u00a05) because it gives M\u00a0&gt;\u00a0Mhalo. That is to say, the unshaded region is $0&lt;\\mathcal {H}&lt;1$.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig7.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/106685863/stx3012fig7.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig7.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"106685863\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/stx3012fig7.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&Signature=kgTEd0WCtDT5YukNVpHTRpy~47z1YvyNE6Lt8sEek4sGBnWeRU8ji6SGx2QMvQYXCmX1d1iGTWGo8qD1CNZN9t~K7yOFm5ha1z3MvNAlfCxVPSmVqi13QOVZty-d0SIXihLCkhS0pkA~CHelDWSYpaig~wdmBK75Fbg1hLY5-XCu4Fx2MkiCWAUn58XXvKH2xXrnYIuj3r2~fxXhtfkcwEdxNP7y41Y0UmoLIfEUD2GqTyTSALXFD1y2teB1EMRP7fRXy1FdLvDR6iRiwUUswNNPchGkRQWuLlqv67AC4UfbF8qN9RpiRKMdECaRCqS7~LXq9mqcmspzTZmdU0BW6A__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=106685863&ar=4655189&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012fig7.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Total mass in the model against the estimated stellar mass, alongside the values for the whole sample. (The labelled orange bars are the systems shown in detail in Figs\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>\u2013<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>.) That is to say, the unshaded region is <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$0&lt;\\mathcal {H}&lt;1$|\u2060</span>.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig7\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 7.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012fig7.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=03YPji~B-f7wgiy7tGSumUmH9Bk8Ox1nzIw2W34AbfSV8sE7X4W~EmgfqHnzciPIIq4izj3thJQkq7BoFhEBS-kMuN8ItRIFFnULENyHa0jmnl3TQInwLOaZCjpiI1tCzfyoa9fgG5r8gTizXN7LuS2NMf49WGMEIdJAs~id3lT~xPRbXr4F5mPMMPSKOU9TDDlZfaBpY3S0-kJXEZ1ZwbgKOKaaSiAvd6d4~QGxicTBQjw5Ey6V55Yj3ZpPIiu-vlV9yYhOKNe6SDESVSmuM4aDLRDVfuctNF-88I5-PBuVDlOi4heIYDYkCFQWEuUcjS6ni19U4PWi-dghQlWGxw__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Total mass in the model against the estimated stellar mass, alongside the values for the whole sample. (The labelled orange bars are the systems shown in detail in Figs\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a>\u2013<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig6\" data-open=\"fig6\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">6</a>.) The horizontal extent of each bar indicates the extreme cases of a young (0.5\u00a0Gyr-old) stellar population and the oldest possible population at the given redshift. The vertical extent indicates the spread of masses in the lens-model ensemble. The lower-right shaded region is unphysical according to the stellar-population models, because it gives <em>M</em>\u00a0&lt;\u00a0<em>M</em><sub>stel</sub>. The upper-left shaded region is unphysical according to abundance matching (see Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>) because it gives <em>M</em>\u00a0&gt;\u00a0<em>M</em><sub>halo</sub>. That is to say, the unshaded region is <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$0&lt;\\mathcal {H}&lt;1$|\u2060</span>.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The halo-matching index expresses whether the lensing mass is plausible given the flux received from the candidate lensing galaxy.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig7\" data-open=\"fig7\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">7</a> and Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> show that most of the candidates have stellar and lensing masses typical of massive ellipticals.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn2\" data-open=\"fn2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">2</a></sup> SW\u200905 is one of the most massive of all the candidates, corresponding to a galaxy-group mass scale. It is a particularly attractive system for follow-up observations at higher resolution, as it is a large system with clear multiple-image features. Modelling leaves little doubt that it is a lens. SW\u200904 seems to be even more massive, but the diagnostics leave some doubts about the validity of this model. The two lowest mass systems, SW\u200919 and SW\u200942, are important if they are indeed lenses, as they would be low-mass lenses dominated by dark matter. All the modelled systems have reasonable stellar-mass fractions, except for two cases where the stellar-mass fraction is too low (<span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">\u2060|$\\mathcal {H}&gt; 1$|\u2060</span>): these are SW\u200942 and SW\u200957. In the case of SW\u200957, the model has poor diagnostics and should be discarded. The model for SW\u200942, on the other hand, is quite convincing \u2013 except for the high halo-matching index. If SW\u200942 turned out not to be a lens, that would support the halo-matching index as an effective criterion to discriminate models.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=106685866 id=\"106685866\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6>6 SUMMARY AND CONCLUSIONS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We report on a first set of mass distributions and follow-up diagnostics for the Space\u2009Warps lens candidates created with a novel approach that aims to be scalable by <em>orders of magnitude</em> to prepare for the many thousands of lenses the next generation of wide-field surveys will yield (e.g. Euclid and WFIRST).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Over the past few years, the way of discovering lenses has changed with the introduction of machine learning and citizen\u2013science methods, combined with the coverage of large areas of the sky by modern surveys. The way lensing mass models are constructed also needs to change, in order to be prepared for the increasing influx of lens candidates. The work in this paper represents a hybrid approach between the classical style, where a small team of experts invests many hours into the creation of a single model, and a citizen\u2013science project, where a crowd of amateur volunteers makes independent contributions. The authors of this paper are a collaboration of professionals and experienced citizen\u2013science volunteers, aiming to create early-stage lens models as soon as a lens candidate is found.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">To assist volunteers in constraining lensing models, we introduce a set of diagnostics that helps us to assess the validity of the models. At a later stage, we encourage modellers to apply those diagnostics as feedback on the plausibility of their assumptions, and to suggest additional diagnostics.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The diagnostics (i)\u2013(iv) (see Section.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a>) turned out to be useful measures of the difficulty in modelling a system, but they did not constitute necessary conditions for a promising model. They can help select systems to introduce novice volunteers to the modelling process. In contrast, diagnostics (v) and (vi) can be considered as necessary criteria for a good model. Volunteers employed those ones to evaluate their models, and turned out to be easy enough to grasp by new volunteers. The halo-matching index diagnostic (vii, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\mathcal {H}$|\u2060</span>) is an interesting criterion that might be useful for the modellers, but needs further investigation.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> is a summary of our results. It characterizes each modelled system with seven diagnostics, indicating (a) the image morphology and how clear or indistinct it is, (b) whether the mass map and synthetic lensed image appear to be plausible, and (c) how the model mass compares with the estimated stellar and full-halo masses. Missing entries are due unavailable imaging data, whereas missing rows are due to models that were not created for this particular candidate.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The trend in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig7\" data-open=\"fig7\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">7</a>, where higher-mass galaxies get progressively more dark-matter dominated, is expected (see e.g. Ferreras, Saha &amp; Williams\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2005</a>), as is the span of about one order of magnitude for the stellar mass and the two orders of magnitude in lensing mass. With future data, it will be interesting to compare the enclosed stellar and lensing mass as a function of radius, going from the star-dominated inner regions to the outer dark haloes. Leier et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>) illustrate this behaviour in their fig. 5, but the present sample could go an order of magnitude higher in mass.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The quick creation of many models for the Space\u2009Warps candidates successfully showed that a subset of citizen scientists is interested in being involved in more challenging tasks that take some time to learn. The next step involves recruiting more lensing enthusiasts, as soon as the next round of Space\u2009Warps is started. In the meantime, the improvements shown in the appendix will be integrated in the standard version of SpaghettiLens. Photometric fitting could also be integrated into SpaghettiLens. This would allow experienced citizen scientists to generate photometric redshifts and stellar masses, and thus generate preliminary dark-matter maps as soon as a lens candidate is identified.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=106685874 id=\"106685874\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title\" >Acknowledgements</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">This work was supported by the University of Zurich Candocreseach grant (Forschungskredit Candoc; FK-14-081 and FK-15-087).</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=106685876 id=\"106685876\" class=\"backfootnotegroup-title\" >Footenotes</h2>\r\n<div content-id=\"fn1\"><span class=\"fn\"><span class=\"label fn-label\"><span rel=\"nofollow\" data-fn-id=\"fn1\" class=\"end-note-link\">1</span></span><div class=\"footnote-content\"><p class=\"footnote-compatibility\"><a class=\"link link-uri openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://labs.spacewarps.org/spaghetti/\" target=\"_blank\">http://labs.spacewarps.org/spaghetti/</a></p></div></span></div><div content-id=\"fn2\"><span class=\"fn\"><span class=\"label fn-label\"><span rel=\"nofollow\" data-fn-id=\"fn2\" class=\"end-note-link\">2</span></span><div class=\"footnote-content\"><p class=\"footnote-compatibility\">The mass values themselves are given in the online version of Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>.</p></div></span></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=106685879 id=\"106685879\" class=\"backreferences-title\" >REFERENCES</h2>\r\n<div class=\"ref-list\"><div content-id=\"bib1\" data-legacy-id=\"bib1\"><div class=\"refLink-parent\"><span class=\"refLink\"><a name=\"jumplink-bib1\" href=\"javascript:;\" aria-label=\"jumplink-bib1\"></a></span></div><div class=\"ref false\"><div id=\"ref-auto-bib1\" class=\"ref-content \"><div class=\"mixed-citation citation\"><p class=\"mixed-citation-compatibility\"><span class=\"person-group\"><span class=\"name string-name\"><div class=\"surname\">Bruderer</div>  <div class=\"given-names\">C.</div></span>, <span class=\"name string-name\"><div class=\"surname\">Read</div>  <div class=\"given-names\">J. N.</div></span> et al.\u00a0</span>, <div class=\"year\">2011</div>, <div class=\"source \">MNRAS</div>, <div class=\"volume\">418</div>, <div class=\"fpage\">1587</div></p><!--citationLinks: case 1--><div class=\"citation-links\"></div><div class=\"citation-links\"><div class=\"crossref-doi js-ref-link\"><a class=\"openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://dx.doi.org/10.1111/j.1365-2966.2011.19536.x\" target=\"_blank\">Crossref</a></div><div class=\"adsDoiReference\"><a class=\"openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/cgi-bin/basic_connect?qsearch=10.1111%2Fj.1365-2966.2011.19536.x\" target=\"_blank\">Search ADS</a></div><div class=\"xslopenurl empty-target\"><span class=\"inst-open-url-holders\" data-targetId=\"10.1111%2Fj.1365-2966.2011.19536.x\"> </span></div>\u00a0</div></div></div></div></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=106685880 id=\"106685880\" class=\"backsection-title\" >SUPPORTING INFORMATION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Supplementary data are available at <em><a class=\"link link-uri openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"https://academic.oup.com/mnras/article-lookup/doi/10.1093/mnras/stx3012#supplementary-data\" target=\"_blank\">MNRAS</a></em> online.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\"><strong>Table\u00a01</strong>. Diagnostics of the selected models for each Space\u2009Warps candidate (see Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec6\"></span><a href=\"#sec6\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">6</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Please note: Oxford University Press is not responsible for the content or functionality of any supporting materials supplied by the authors. Any queries (other than missing material) should be directed to the corresponding author for the article.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=106685885 id=\"106685885\" class=\"appendix-title\" data-legacy-id=sec7>APPENDIX A: DEVELOPMENTS IN SPAGHETTILENS</h3>\r\n                    <h4 scrollto-destination=106685886 id=\"106685886\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec7-1>A1 Improved synthetic images</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The mass maps produced by the current implementation of SpaghettiLens are based on images of point-like features. No information about extended images is used, except in so far as they help the user identify images of point-like features. The synthetic images offered to users are rudimentary, corresponding to conical light profiles (i.e. circular light profiles with brightness decreasing linearly with radius).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We have now developed a prototype to improve the generation of synthetic images, as illustrated in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-figa1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"figa1\" data-open=\"figa1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">A1</a>. Areas containing lensed images are selected (green frames in the figure). The selected areas should be as free as possible from other sources, including the lensing galaxy. Pixels within the selected areas are mapped to a grid on the source plane, using bending angles given by the mass model. The mapping from lens-plane pixels to source-plane grid cells is many-to-one, because of image multiplicity and magnification. The brightness of each source-plane pixel is set to the mean of all the lens-plane pixels mapped to it. Finally, the mapping is run back to the lens plane. The result is a synthetic image. In effect, one is reconstructing a source-plane brightness map by least squares.</p>                        <a id=\"106685889\" scrollto-destination=\"106685889\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"figa1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure A1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012figa1.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=VHgsmZqJJZ7SPLd2crrTQ71UsZ3WcQ23f91-AlGVmS5EEh5UAc9PaeFr5P7~kZ6p62snWuF3nZcJXmeokzz1vmHZmkmTpm5i0IJ96qNxA-xd7xYLuL-SSenY8n-EvxGdA3xvs3xeLuxJek5ZN4HBlh2kY9pge5~0XPJ4bWr4Wd6qmAcoze92LyoV7cN8YTsgxZGdCWvurGodX7rmmiNgHUIDQ9lFnSoYqZsm2EkZOFsu-Ils0pGmwF13YCIEsua1DjX0Dl18tHpK9DkI0LHiyym3pjf4Eyrh6GJdJbbbSPqRFF3rs6~~WrGX77p5sd6hP~15Yr4lxju09mfJiahjMg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Synthetic lensed image with source-profile fitting in SW05 (J143454.4+522850). Top-left: original image, with areas containing lensed images enclosed within green frames. Top-right: synthetic image (coloured arcs) with lensing galaxy and unrelated objects in grey-scale. Bottom from left to right: reconstructed source in colour, intensity (grey-scale), count of lens-plane pixels per source-plane pixel, and residual of original image to synthetic image.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012figa1.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/106685889/stx3012figa1.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012figa1.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"106685889\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/stx3012figa1.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&Signature=FVc~Arq6XV7GFdwxu~4Vdxap1m7w7Ki-HR9PJkGRYUltg2g6YnQpoG2Ti8J8ZGssx~95bLrX5j2xpWpeR--um5AvoJhHG8iL68Flvk3YNEq0OjGFdiK~hyAMOK29ZNg0Q3u9Uh7bmnel9ESjsIlG5g6o2WIPDldAje1CZ5BS6R8rFwT00kL~YD7-4kGe4xmA-ZtA1yJfD8Dtg-W6VRY~UPvLt6K0xRZZ6rusirG04ndsUFsbJagD1oZbW8ThVgmIcKi5RJHHGIQ5a1uVwAfeWdlXTLxwbY~TyHmv2V0miARlkldIBG9Fu~GbqZ7pqFTwYm0AIsVoJc-8hlUdo2mC7Q__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=106685889&ar=4655189&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012figa1.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Synthetic lensed image with source-profile fitting in SW05 (J143454.4+522850). Bottom from left to right: reconstructed source in colour, intensity (grey-scale), count of lens-plane pixels per source-plane pixel, and residual of original image to synthetic image.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"figa1\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure A1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012figa1.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=VHgsmZqJJZ7SPLd2crrTQ71UsZ3WcQ23f91-AlGVmS5EEh5UAc9PaeFr5P7~kZ6p62snWuF3nZcJXmeokzz1vmHZmkmTpm5i0IJ96qNxA-xd7xYLuL-SSenY8n-EvxGdA3xvs3xeLuxJek5ZN4HBlh2kY9pge5~0XPJ4bWr4Wd6qmAcoze92LyoV7cN8YTsgxZGdCWvurGodX7rmmiNgHUIDQ9lFnSoYqZsm2EkZOFsu-Ils0pGmwF13YCIEsua1DjX0Dl18tHpK9DkI0LHiyym3pjf4Eyrh6GJdJbbbSPqRFF3rs6~~WrGX77p5sd6hP~15Yr4lxju09mfJiahjMg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Synthetic lensed image with source-profile fitting in SW05 (J143454.4+522850). Bottom from left to right: reconstructed source in colour, intensity (grey-scale), count of lens-plane pixels per source-plane pixel, and residual of original image to synthetic image.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012figa1.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/106685889/stx3012figa1.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012figa1.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"106685889\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/stx3012figa1.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&Signature=FVc~Arq6XV7GFdwxu~4Vdxap1m7w7Ki-HR9PJkGRYUltg2g6YnQpoG2Ti8J8ZGssx~95bLrX5j2xpWpeR--um5AvoJhHG8iL68Flvk3YNEq0OjGFdiK~hyAMOK29ZNg0Q3u9Uh7bmnel9ESjsIlG5g6o2WIPDldAje1CZ5BS6R8rFwT00kL~YD7-4kGe4xmA-ZtA1yJfD8Dtg-W6VRY~UPvLt6K0xRZZ6rusirG04ndsUFsbJagD1oZbW8ThVgmIcKi5RJHHGIQ5a1uVwAfeWdlXTLxwbY~TyHmv2V0miARlkldIBG9Fu~GbqZ7pqFTwYm0AIsVoJc-8hlUdo2mC7Q__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=106685889&ar=4655189&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012figa1.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Synthetic lensed image with source-profile fitting in SW05 (J143454.4+522850). Top-left: original image, with areas containing lensed images enclosed within green frames. Top-right: synthetic image (coloured arcs) with lensing galaxy and unrelated objects in grey-scale. Bottom from left to right: reconstructed source in colour, intensity (grey-scale), count of lens-plane pixels per source-plane pixel, and residual of original image to synthetic image.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The procedure is not yet implemented in SpaghettiLens but can be applied during post-processing. The new synthetic images could be used to improve the mass reconstruction, by weighing the ensemble of maps according to how good the synthetic images are.</p>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=106685891 id=\"106685891\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec7-2>A2 Sub-sampling of the central region</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The models of simulated lenses in K\u00fcng et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>) showed a tendency to produce density profiles which were too shallow, resulting typically in overestimates of the Einstein radius. Allowing some extra mass tiles in central region, thus allowing the mass profile to rise more steeply near the centre, was suggested as a possible cure.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-figa2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"figa2\" data-open=\"figa2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">A2</a> shows an experiment with smaller mass tiles in the inner region. Replacing the very central mass tile with nine smaller tiles allows for steeper central profiles. Doing the same for the 25 innermost mass tiles allows for even steeper central profiles, eliminating the systematic shallow profiles. However, it does not provide a completely satisfactory solution, because (a) it increases the number of mass tiles by 40\u2009per\u2009cent and significantly increases the computational time, and (b) the square boundary between areas with different tile sizes is rather undesirable. The main modelling work in this paper was, however, done before the experiment with smaller mass tiles was complete. Some of the models presented in this paper apply the intermediate option (corresponding to the middle panel in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-figa2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"figa2\" data-open=\"figa2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">A2</a>) while others use the old system. We note this paper mainly concerns the enclosed mass in the outer regions, so shallowness in the central region should not be an issue.</p>                        <a id=\"106685894\" scrollto-destination=\"106685894\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"figa2\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure A2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012figa2.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=X05cU8pCn3qwXoqXb~fkTHPDG0UTBjPThKayNYFvOCZZ2GHKBlC2Oh5fY4EolubURm4M5MaGWCzjBRxx56glW~LzBGEtwD8SL8Z-tF2X40BywxlerhlgNUyHd2tSHgCBJRBbVMR3oJaUjkB0gvza8S52ocVuHGona46~fq~lK6r2kY622h0vm1ChR-0NLQqcRZSQsnY0Hd3P3DWy7CO4c2W7Y1JBpfiWN2oOrp~V0~Q4TEMPh7NaqcV85eqzbKVOVccfZcU3iOPz5zMCasr2XUDMhaCQPLIE8~3uMZI8nnm6VobNxQZRrpx~XnT2wAulPUaYFl7P8XPiCABkwB~8nA__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Model improvement resulting from the use of smaller mass tiles in the inner region of the mass model. The middle panel is the result when the innermost mass tile is replaced by nine smaller tiles. The lower panel results from replacing the innermost 5 \u00d7 5 tiles with nine smaller tiles each.</p></div></div>                    <h4 scrollto-destination=106685895 id=\"106685895\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec7-3>A3 Parametrization of pixel models</h4>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In order to fit the set of pixelated models to a single parametrized model, a program was written that took a parametrized function and subtracted from it the mean and the principal components (PCs) of the data. This created the residual function. The number of PCs in the analysis was varied, to test how this affected the output. It was found that five PCs gave a reasonable approximation. A masking function was added, selecting only the data points that fell inside the image of the lens, and the PCs were clipped in order to keep the values inside the region of the ensemble. Any value higher than the clip was set to be the clip value. This was chosen to 2.5 because, assuming that the data follow a Gaussian error distribution, almost all the values for the variance should lie between 2 and 3 standard deviations from the mean. Minimizing the residuals function produces the set of parameters that fit the parametrized function to the original pixelated ensemble most closely. A least squares fit was used to perform this minimization. The parametrized model function was obtained from the gravitational potential of an isothermal ellipsoid mass distribution (Keeton\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>). This model is frequently used to describe gravitational lenses, giving good fits to the observations. The isothermal ellipsoid model outputs three useful parameters: the radius of the Einstein ring, the ellipticity of the model and the angle of the ellipticity from the vertical, giving the orientation of the galaxy. By applying this model to simulated lenses for which the values of these parameters were already known, it was possible to assess the accuracy of the methodology, before applying the model to the candidate lensing galaxies. Preliminary results on the recovery of Einstein radii are shown in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-figa3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"figa3\" data-open=\"figa3\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">A3</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"106685897\" scrollto-destination=\"106685897\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"figa3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure A3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/m_stx3012figa3.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&amp;Signature=3A27KSDHNssxrl0J5Cyciulf5R3CxCMOMMzQecp4ADbS4U1fVuEX~1jg8GVJYHsHvaoLNkahhJ7Ae1~zsCHdNYQaPfi6YW-AiM-j4zwBcjfa4fOKe9ElUp4evdjVsA7gbLpDWetPRBRFvNIKHT9Zdu8UnMXNGPAdYdKHsCnwiT9o-zKgUsRCEkFlbS68B4ekC3MOSFFX7zomqBemB5QTF0tfSj5onIMRPPQ0yUnlASZETybbseRxkRhc5EVa2pNfLgwfIu79vu6JwPanVrbA4DByO-QqxJXTNg8JQJdS2xievQyrAoIojRF-05Vi1Vy~q6lbMQWUEhPznUgcQMgJng__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Comparison of Einstein radii rE obtained from mass tiles to the results from a parametrized model to test the performance of the algorithm. The parametrized model was generated using principal component analysis on the ensemble of models. The blue dashed line represents a perfect recovery of rE.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012figa3.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/106685897/stx3012figa3.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012figa3.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"106685897\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/474/3/10.1093_mnras_stx3012/1/stx3012figa3.jpeg?Expires=1611466367&Signature=RSnfJBlqweeq9bbUtEb3ZdhIiDlSoMOmtCRVHWcWhvuX0FAPFoxeVwIqNtx3bEJPDS~~IQVMK9vvjpxQ9DV6QmN76Xlg-tN-SROyzpbl8QbjFCCq7~uhLRaJyZkNbYNpx-~4UpD4AXBdrjTCHVQi8ibH~R-6OxY5wc7YgdAcAE46SFEsc5zPpXQgLJW-Wtw~DwZIMTxONmeGtu0hZ3W4tWHWF746SX4MJ31w~VFoLQXy29nlR5tvfZpxC8hFjuhGW9pEHdxLAo~VxcwrnqrUW8QskFbcNLJIr2bY~MAmNy5sKpg8MwnuHVekpl2R4nHZiumHVYOzrUr7bShZzopF3w__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=106685897&ar=4655189&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stx3012figa3.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Comparison of Einstein radii <em>r</em><sub>E</sub> obtained from mass tiles to the results from a parametrized model to test the performance of the algorithm. Space\u2009Warps was ongoing. Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a> shows the total number of models generated since launch for our lens candidates. A small number of volunteers started creating models of possible lens candidates from Space\u2009Warps that were debated in the discussion forum. In the beginning of 2013 August (around day 70 since release), a modelling challenge for the candidate later to be identified as SW\u200901 was launched. A group of five volunteers presented their results in an online letter converging on a set of 30 models. In 2015 April (day 700), the first major version of SpaghettiLens was released. At the same time, the list of identified candidates was made available (as a preprint of More et\u00a0al.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). At this stage, the volunteers were asked to create models for all the lens candidates that were still missing. The work done for candidate SW\u200929 shows that the volunteers converged on a favourable model much faster, after 15 models, generated in 30\u2009d. The total modelling effort resulted in a set of 377 SpaghettiLens models for all but one of the 59 Space\u2009Warps lens candidates; candidate SW\u200939 was not modelled by any volunteer. Over its runtime, the system logged eight major contributors (defined as volunteers that generated, at least, five models)."}, "Pandas format": {"Table 2": {"Status": "Complete", "Action": "Processed "Monthly Notices of the Royal Astronomical Society", "volume": "474", "publication_year": "2018/03/1", "start_page": "3700", "end_page": "3713", "keywords": ["gravitational lensing: strong", "galaxies: general", "galaxies: stellar content", "dark matter", "Astrophysics - Astrophysics of Galaxies"], "url": "https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2018MNRAS.474.3700K", "abstract": "We report modelling follow-up of recently discovered gravitational-lens candidates in the Canada France Hawaii Telescope Legacy Survey. Lens modelling was done by a small group of specially interested volunteers from the Space Warps citizen-science community who originally found the candidate lenses. Models are categorized according to seven diagnostics indicating (a) the image morphology and how clear or indistinct it is, (b) whether the mass map and synthetic lensed image appear to be plausible, and (c) how the lens-model mass compares with the stellar mass and the abundance-matched halo mass. The lensing masses range from \u223c10<SUP>11</SUP> to &gt;10<SUP>13</SUP> M<SUB>\u2609</SUB>. Preliminary estimates of the stellar masses show a smaller spread in stellar mass (except for two lenses): a factor of a few below or above \u223c10<SUP>11</SUP> M<SUB>\u2609</SUB>. Therefore, we expect the stellar-to-total mass fraction to decline sharply as lensing mass increases. The most massive system with a convincing model is J1434+522 (SW 05). The two low-mass outliers are J0206-095 (SW 19) and J2217+015 (SW 42); if these two are indeed lenses, they probe an interesting regime of very low star formation efficiency. Some improvements to the modelling software (SpaghettiLens), and discussion of strategies regarding scaling to future surveys with more and frequent discoveries, are included.", "doi": "10.1093/mnras/stx3012", "custom1": "eprint: arXiv:1711.07297", "issn": "0035-8711", "number": "3"}, "Inspection status": "Incomplete"}
